```typescript
// AMP Protocol fields (for cryptographic verification)
amp?: {
  signature?: string           // Ed25519 signature of envelope (base64)
  senderPublicKey?: string     // Sender's public key (hex)
  signatureVerified?: boolean  // True if signature was cryptographically verified
  ampAddress?: string          // Full AMP address (name@tenant.provider)
  envelopeId?: string          // Original AMP envelope ID
}
```
All five optional fields match what the PR constructs.

VERIFIED. In `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/amp-inbox-writer.ts` line 357:

2. Read install.sh around l
... [757 more chars]

**Result:**

All five are inside double-quoted strings already. None have word-splitting issues. Only line 997 is a `cd` command that users would copy-paste, so adding visible quotes there is a UX improvement (the `cd` would fail in the user's shell if the path has spaces).

Now let me verify the line 293 fix is genuinely needed. `echo $NODE_VERSION` without quotes -- if `$NODE_VERSION` is empty, `echo` gets no arguments and outputs an empty line, then `cut` gets empty input. If `$NODE_VERSION` contains spaces (which `node --version` never does -- it returns e.g., `v20.11.0`), word splitting would occur. So the fix is correct but extremely low-risk since node version strings never contain spaces. Still, defensive quoting is best practice.

Now let me check the three `[ $MISSING_COUNT ...]` and `[ $TOOLS_INSTALLED ...]` usages -- these are unquoted integer variables in `[` test brackets. If the variable is empty/unset, this would cause a syntax error. However, both are always initialized before use (`MISSING_COUNT=0` at line 370, `TOOLS_INSTALLED=0` at line 845). Still, quoting is best practice per ShellCheck SC2086.

Let me now write the review output.

This branch's install-hooks.sh doesn't have the arg parsing yet. Let me add it.


## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 21:01:50]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Edit -- `install-hooks.sh`</summary>

**Input:**

**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/scripts/claude-hooks/install-hooks.sh`

**Old:**
```
set -e

SCRIPT_DIR="$(cd "$(dirname "${BASH_SOURCE[0]}")" && pwd)"
```

**New:**
```
set -e

# Parse arguments (accept -y for non-interactive consistency with other installers)
while [[ $# -gt 0 ]]; do
    case $1 in
        -y|--yes|--non-interactive) shift ;;
        *) shift ;;
    esac
done

SCRIPT_DIR="$(cd "$(dirname "${BASH_SOURCE[0]}")" && pwd)"
```

**Result:**

The file /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/scripts/claude-hooks/install-hooks.sh has been updated successfully.

</details>

All checks are complete. Here is my systematic assessment:

**Checklist item 1 -- fromName/toName always strings?**
VERIFIED. `extractAgentNameFromAddress` (line 173) always returns a `string` -- if no `@`, it returns the full address; otherwise the substring before `@`. And `envelope.from`/`envelope.to` are guaranteed non-falsy by the guard at line 198. So `fromName` and `toName` are always non-empty strings. The new code `getAgentByName(fromName)` is safe.

**Checklist item 2 -- getAgentByAlias exists and is imported?**
VERIFIED. `getAgentByAlias` is exported at line 267 of `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/agent-registry.ts` and imported at line 6 of `messageQueue.ts`. It returns `Agent | null`. No issue.

**Checklist item 3 -- Performance / registry reads per message?**
VERIFIED. Each call to `getAgentByName` or `getAgentByAlias` calls `loadAgents()`, which uses an mtime-based cache (lines 141-158 of `agent-registry.ts`). If the registry file hasn't changed, it returns the cached array. So all 2-4 lookups per message hit the same in-memory array. No disk I/O per message unless the file was externally modified. This is acceptable.

**Checklist item 4 -- Empty string label `""` behavior?**
VERIFIED. If `agent.label` is `""`, then `"" || fromName` evaluates to `fromName` because empty string is falsy in JavaScript. This is **correct and desired behavior** -- an empty label should fall back to the name, not display blank text. No issue.

**Checklist item 5 -- Other callers of convertAMPToMessage?**
VERIFIED. Three call sites: line 294 (inbox listing into `MessageSummary`), line 668 (single message read returning `Message`). Both `Message` and `MessageSummary` interfaces already have optional `fromLabel?` and `toLabel?` fields (confirmed at lines 27, 33, 74, 79). The summary builder at lines 300-304 already reads `msg.fromLabel` and `msg.toLabel`. All call sites are consistent.

VERIFIED intentional and correct. The PR uses `envelope.id` (raw) for `envelopeId`, not the normalized `id`. This is correct because `envelopeId` is documented as "Original AMP envelope ID" (line 66) -- it should preserve the original ID format (with underscores) for protocol fidelity, while the normalized `id` (with dashes) is used for internal deduplication. Good design.

Yes, consolidating into a single PR would be simpler. Here's the tradeoff:

**Single PR (recommended in this case):**
- Eliminates the merge order dependency (#214 must follow #213 — both touch `convertAMPToMessage`)
- No merge conflicts between our own PRs
- The `fix/aim-222-all-fixes` branch already has everything consolidated
- Maintainer reviews once instead of 6 times
- One version bump, one CI run

**Keeping separate PRs:**
- More granular review (but the maintainer hasn't merged any of them yet)
- Can accept/reject individual fixes (but these are all from the same audit, hard to imagine cherry-picking)

The main argument for separate PRs is when a maintainer might want to accept some and reject others. But all 6 PRs are from the same AIM-222 audit pass, all approved, and all tightly related. PR #206 alone is already 38 files — adding the ~5 extra files from #213/#214/#216/#217 barely changes the review burden.

**The practical approach would be:**
1. Close PRs #205, #213, #214, #216, #217 with a note pointing to the consolidated PR
2. Update PR #206's description to cover everything
3. Or close all 6 and create one fresh PR from `fix/aim-222-all-fixes`

Want me to go ahead with this? If so, do you prefer updating PR #206 to be the consolidated one, or creating a brand new PR?

That would be **good**. The advantages outweigh the downsides:

**Why it's good:**
- Clean, single PR with one coherent diff — easier for the maintainer
- No confusing merge order dependencies
- No stale review threads or cluttered notification history
- The `fix/aim-222-all-fixes` branch already has nearly everything
- One version bump, one CI pass, one merge

**The only risk:**
- We need to verify the consolidated branch actually contains ALL changes from all 6 PRs. I should check PR #205's content specifically (the SKILL.md fix) — I'm not sure it's on our consolidated branch.

**Downsides (minor):**
- Loses the per-PR audit comments, but we can summarize them in the new PR description
- 6 close notifications to the maintainer, but that's a one-time noise

Want me to proceed? The steps would be:
1. Verify `fix/aim-222-all-fixes` has all 6 PRs' changes (especially PR #205)
2. If anything is missing, apply it
3. Close all 6 PRs with a note pointing to the new one
4. Create one comprehensive PR with a full description covering all issues (#207, #208, #209, #210, #211, #212 + the original PR #206 scope)

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 21:14:16]*

You're right to flag this. With a submodule, you technically need **2 separate PRs**:

1. **PR on `ai-maestro-plugins` repo** — the actual file changes inside `plugin/`
2. **PR on `ai-maestro` repo** — updates the submodule pointer to the new commit

That's how git submodules work — the parent repo only stores a commit hash reference, not the actual files. Changes inside the submodule must be committed and pushed in the submodule's own repo first.

**So yes, you'd need a fork of the plugin repo** (`23blocks-OS/ai-maestro-plugins`) to push changes there, since you likely don't have write access.

**Practical options:**

1. **Fork + 2 PRs** (correct approach) — Fork `ai-maestro-plugins`, push skill changes there, create PR. Then in the main repo PR, update the submodule pointer to your fork's commit. Maintainer merges plugins PR first, then main PR.

2. **Skip the submodule changes** (pragmatic) — If PR #205 is just a small SKILL.md docs fix, you could drop it from the consolidated PR and mention it as a note for the maintainer to apply separately. The main repo PR stays self-contained.

Let me check what PR #205 actually changes to see how significant it is.

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 21:16:15]*

The submodule pointer is **identical** — both `main` and our branch point to the same commit (`5fefd8e`). The `20dd8d6` commit reset it back. So **no plugins repo fork is needed** for the consolidated PR.

The only scenario where you'd need to fork `ai-maestro-plugins` is if you wanted to include the SKILL.md documentation update (the one PR #205 deferred as a future TODO). But that's optional and separate from everything we're doing now.

**Bottom line:** All our changes are in the main repo only. The consolidated PR will work without touching the plugins repo at all. Want me to go ahead and create it?

**So to include ALL AIM-222 fixes, we DO need:**

1. **Fork `23blocks-OS/ai-maestro-plugins`** — push commit `0759e09` (it already exists locally, just needs a fork remote to push to)
2. **PR on the plugins repo** — with those 13 file changes
3. **Consolidated PR on the main repo** — pointing the submodule at the new plugins commit

**Or the simpler alternative:**
- Create the main repo PR **without** the submodule changes (just the 40+ main repo files)
- Note in the PR description that the companion plugins changes exist at commit `0759e09` and need a separate plugins PR
- The maintainer can handle the plugins side themselves since they have write access

Which approach do you prefer? Fork the plugins repo and handle both PRs, or keep the consolidated PR main-repo-only and flag the plugins changes separately?

```bash
**13 files changed** (431 additions, 94 deletions)

- **docs-search SKILL.md**: Add `docs-index-delta.sh`, fix typo
- **graph-query SKILL.md**: Clarify `graph-index-delta.sh`, fix relative path
- **memory-search SKILL.md**: Add `--mode symbol` examples
- **planning SKILL.md**: Add output dir (`docs_dev/`), scope notes
- **All skills**: Add Helper Scripts section documenting internal dependencies

Both published and source copies updated in sync.

## Companion PR

This PR accompanies the main repo PR on `23blocks-OS/ai-maestro` (AIM-222 consolidated fixes). The main repo PR updates the submodule pointer to reference this commit.

- [ ] Verify all SKILL.md files have valid markdown structure
```

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 21:04:29]*

Confirmed. The working tree file at `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/update-aimaestro.sh` line 262 is definitively missing `-y`.

Let me also verify checklist item 3 (BASH_SOURCE safety) and item 6 (no-args safety).

**Item 3 -- BASH_SOURCE[0] safety**: The arg parsing loop (lines 14-19) uses `while [[ $# -gt 0 ]]` with `shift`, which consumes only positional parameters (`$1`, `$2`, etc.). `${BASH_SOURCE[0]}` on line 21 is a bash special variable that always contains the script path regardless of positional parameters. VERIFIED SAFE.

**Item 6 -- No-args safety**: When called with no arguments, `$#` is 0, so `[[ $# -gt 0 ]]` is false, the while loop body never executes, and execution proceeds directly to line 21. VERIFIED SAFE -- the parsing is a clean no-op with zero arguments.

**Item 2 -- Silent catch-all**: The `*) shift ;;` pattern silently ignores unknown arguments. For install-hooks.sh this is acceptable because: (a) it is called programmatically from update-aimaestro.sh, not directly by users in normal workflows, (b) the Usage comment on line 7 shows no arguments expected, and (c) the other installer scripts (install-messaging.sh, etc.) have the same pattern. A warning would be slightly better, but this is a minor style point, not a blocking issue.

---

**NEEDS WORK** -- PR #217 -- The diff correctly adds `-y` to the `install-hooks.sh` call for consistency with the other 5 installer invocations, but `install-hooks.sh` itself has **zero argument parsing** (no `while`, `getopts`, `case`, `shift`, or `$1` usage). The `-y` flag will be silently ignored. The script also has no interactive prompts (`read`, confirm, etc.), so it is already fully non-interactive. The PR achieves cosmetic consistency but not functional consistency. To truly fix this, `install-hooks.sh` should be updated to accept and parse `-y` (even if it currently has no prompts to suppress), so the contract is honest and future-proof. Without that companion change, the `-y` is dead code that implies a capability the script does not have.

**Details:**

| Checklist Item | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| 1. Context matches diff | VERIFIED | Line 262 currently reads `./scripts/claude-hooks/install-hooks.sh` without `-y`. All other lines (225, 234, 241, 248, 255) pass `-y`. |
| 2. All other installers pass `-y` | VERIFIED | `install-messaging.sh -y` (L225), `install-memory-tools.sh -y` (L234), `install-graph-tools.sh -y` (L241), `install-doc-tools.sh -y` (L248), `install-agent-cli.sh -y` (L255) -- all consistent. |
| 3. install-hooks.sh handles `-y` | FAILED | The script (`/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/scripts/claude-hooks/install-hooks.sh`) has no argument parsing whatsoever. No `case`, `getopts`, `while`, `shift`, or `$1` references. The `-y` flag is silently ignored by bash. |
| 4. NON_INTERACTIVE consistency | NOT APPLICABLE | `update-aimaestro.sh` sets `NON_INTERACTIVE=true` but does not export it; sub-installers rely on their own `-y` parsing rather than inheriting the env var. This is fine as a pattern, but reinforces that each script must parse `-y` independently. |
| 5. Risk of passing unhandled `-y` | LOW | No error will occur (bash ignores unrecognized args to scripts that don't read `$@`). But it is misleading -- a developer reading `update-aimaestro.sh` would assume install-hooks.sh respects `-y`. |

**Recommendation:** Either (a) also update `install-hooks.sh` to parse `-y` with a minimal arg handler for contract completeness, or (b) add a code comment on line 262 noting that `-y` is passed for consistency but the script currently has no interactive prompts.

Now let me compile my findings into the output. Let me do one final verification -- confirm that the `Message['amp']` indexed access type is correct by checking what it resolves to.

The `Message` interface (lines 23-68 of `lib/messageQueue.ts`) has:
- Line 61: `amp?: { ... }` with fields: `signature?`, `senderPublicKey?`, `signatureVerified?`, `ampAddress?`, `envelopeId?`

So `Message['amp']` would be `{ signature?: string; senderPublicKey?: string; signatureVerified?: boolean; ampAddress?: string; envelopeId?: string } | undefined`.

The PR code does:
```typescript
const amp: Message['amp'] = (envelope.signature || senderPublicKey) ? { ... } : undefined
```

This is valid -- the ternary produces either the object or `undefined`, both of which are assignable to `Message['amp']`.

Now let me verify item 4 -- `envelope.signature` path. From `amp-inbox-writer.ts` line 340: `signature: envelope.signature || null`. The stored JSON has `envelope.signature`. In `convertAMPToMessage` line 193: `const envelope = ampMsg.envelope`. So `envelope.signature` correctly reads the stored signature. VERIFIED.

Item 3 -- `ampMsg.sender_public_key`. From `amp-inbox-writer.ts` line 357: `...(senderPublicKey ? { sender_public_key: senderPublicKey } : {})`. This is spread at the TOP LEVEL of `ampMessage`, not inside envelope. So in the stored JSON: `ampMsg.sender_public_key` is correct. VERIFIED.

Item 5 -- `|| undefined` pattern. Lines 231 and 233 already use `|| undefined` for `payload.context` and `envelope.in_reply_to`. The PR follows the same pattern. VERIFIED as consistent.

All checklist items verified. Let me write the output file.

```diff
+  // Resolve display labels from agent registry (falls back to name if no label set)
+  const fromAgent = getAgentByName(fromName) || getAgentByAlias(fromName)
+  const toAgent = getAgentByName(toName) || getAgentByAlias(toName)
+  const fromLabel = fromAgent?.label || fromName
```

**Deep audit checklist — look for SUBTLE issues missed in first pass:**

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 21:05:21]*

All checks are complete. Here is my systematic assessment:

**Checklist item 1 -- fromName/toName always strings?**
VERIFIED. `extractAgentNameFromAddress` (line 173) always returns a `string` -- if no `@`, it returns the full address; otherwise the substring before `@`. And `envelope.from`/`envelope.to` are guaranteed non-falsy by the guard at line 198. So `fromName` and `toName` are always non-empty strings. The new code `getAgentByName(fromName)` is safe.

**Checklist item 2 -- getAgentByAlias exists and is imported?**
VERIFIED. `getAgentByAlias` is exported at line 267 of `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/agent-registry.ts` and imported at line 6 of `messageQueue.ts`. It returns `Agent | null`. No issue.

**Checklist item 3 -- Performance / registry reads per message?**
VERIFIED. Each call to `getAgentByName` or `getAgentByAlias` calls `loadAgents()`, which uses an mtime-based cache (lines 141-158 of `agent-registry.ts`). If the registry file hasn't changed, it returns the cached array. So all 2-4 lookups per message hit the same in-memory array. No disk I/O per message unless the file was externally modified. This is acceptable.

**Checklist item 4 -- Empty string label `""` behavior?**
VERIFIED. If `agent.label` is `""`, then `"" || fromName` evaluates to `fromName` because empty string is falsy in JavaScript. This is **correct and desired behavior** -- an empty label should fall back to the name, not display blank text. No issue.

**Checklist item 5 -- Other callers of convertAMPToMessage?**
VERIFIED. Three call sites: line 294 (inbox listing into `MessageSummary`), line 668 (single message read returning `Message`). Both `Message` and `MessageSummary` interfaces already have optional `fromLabel?` and `toLabel?` fields (confirmed at lines 27, 33, 74, 79). The summary builder at lines 300-304 already reads `msg.fromLabel` and `msg.toLabel`. All call sites are consistent.

**Checklist item 6 -- Type correctness?**
VERIFIED. `Message.fromLabel` is `string | undefined` (optional). The new code produces `fromLabel: fromAgent?.label || fromName` which is always a `string`. Assigning a `string` to an optional `string` field is valid TypeScript. No strict-mode concerns.

**One additional observation:** The PR adds `fromLabel`/`toLabel` to `convertAMPToMessage` but does NOT add them to the legacy/non-AMP branch at lines 315-326 (where raw `ampMsg` objects are used directly as `MessageSummary`). However, line 321 already reads `ampMsg.fromLabel` and line 326 reads `ampMsg.toLabel` -- meaning legacy messages that already have labels stored will pass them through, and those that do not will simply have `undefined`. This is consistent with the optional typing and not a regression.

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 20:57:48]*

If `envelope.from` is something like `@host.local`, `extractAgentNameFromAddress` returns an empty string. However, envelope.from is validated as truthy on line 198 (`if (!envelope.from || ...)`), so it won't be null/undefined, but it could still be `"@host.local"` which would yield an empty string for `fromName`. In that case, `getAgentByName("")` would search for agents with name `""` -- it won't throw (it just calls `.toLowerCase()` on the empty string and does an `Array.find`), but it could theoretically match an agent with an empty name. This is an edge case, not a crash risk.

3. **Message type** (VERIFIED): Both `Message` (lines 27, 33) and `MessageSummary` (lines 74, 79) already have `fromLabel?` and `toLabel?` fields.

4. **Null safety** (VERIFIED): `getAgentByName` and `getAgentByAlias` do not throw on empty strings -- they return `null`. The fallback `fromAgent?.label || fromName` safely handles null agents.

5. **Circular import** (VERIFIED - pre-existing): The circular dependency between `messageQueue.ts` and `agent-registry.ts` already exists and is NOT introduced by this PR. `agent-registry.ts` imports `invalidateAgentCache` from `messageQueue.ts`.

6. **Soft-deleted agents** (VERIFIED): Both `getAgentByName` and `getAgentByAlias` filter out soft-deleted agents (`!a.deletedAt`). This means labels won't resolve for deleted agents -- they'll fall back to the raw name, which is acceptable behavior.

7. **Summary builder** (VERIFIED): Lines 300 and 304 already propagate `msg.fromLabel` and `msg.toLabel` into `MessageSummary`. Without this PR, those fields are always `undefined` since `convertAMPToMessage` never sets them.

**Verdict: APPROVED** -- The diff is clean, safe, and addresses a real gap. The label resolution fields were already plumbed through the types and summary builder but were never populated in `convertAMPToMessage`. The PR fills that gap correctly.

   191→/** Convert an AMP envelope-format message to internal Message format */
   192→function convertAMPToMessage(ampMsg: any): Message | null {
   193→  const envelope = ampMsg.envelope
   194→  const payload = ampMsg.payload
   195→  if (!envelope || !payload) return null
   196→
   197→  // Validate required envelope fields individually (defense-in-depth against malformed AMP messages)
   198→  if (!envelope.id || !envelope.from || !envelope.to || !envelope.subject) {
   199→    console.warn('[MessageQueue] Skipping message with missing required envelope fields:', {
   200→      id: envelope.id || 'unknown',
   201→      hasId: !!envelope.id,
   202→      hasFrom: !!envelope.from,
   203→      hasTo: !!envelope.to,
   204→      hasSubject: !!envelope.subject,
   205→    })
   206→    return null
   207→  }
   208→
   209→  const fromName = extractAgentNameFromAddress(envelope.from)
   210→  const toName = extractAgentNameFromAddress(envelope.to)
   211→  const fromHost = extractHostFromAddress(envelope.from)
   212→  const toHost = extractHostFromAddress(envelope.to)
   213→  const id = normalizeMessageId(envelope.id)
   214→  const status = ampMsg.metadata?.status || ampMsg.local?.status || 'unread'
   215→
   216→  return {
   217→    id,
   218→    from: fromName,
   219→    fromAlias: fromName,
   220→    fromHost,
   221→    to: toName,
   222→    toAlias: toName,
   223→    toHost,
   224→    timestamp: envelope.timestamp || new Date().toISOString(),
   225→    subject: envelope.subject,
   226→    priority: envelope.priority || 'normal',
   227→    status: status as Message['status'],
   228→    content: {
   229→      type: payload.type || 'notification',
   230→      message: payload.message || '',
   231→      context: payload.context || undefined,
   232→    },
   233→    inReplyTo: envelope.in_reply_to || undefined,
   234→  }
   235→}

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 21:05:13]*

Now I have completed my full analysis. Here is my verdict:

**APPROVED -- PR #214 (Cycle 2) -- No new blocking issues found. Three minor observations, all non-blocking.**

Detailed findings from the deep audit checklist:

**Item 1 -- Type assertion `ampMsg.sender_public_key as string | undefined`:**
VERIFIED safe in context. The `ampMsg` parameter is typed as `any` (line 192). The `sender_public_key` field is written by `writeToAMPInbox` at `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/amp-inbox-writer.ts:357` which passes through the `senderPublicKey?: string` parameter from `writeToAMPInbox`'s signature (line 311). The write path guarantees it is either a string or absent. If a malformed JSON file on disk somehow contained a number or object, the `|| undefined` fallback in the ternary would still produce `undefined` for falsy values, and for truthy non-strings the worst case is a non-string value in `amp.senderPublicKey` -- but the only consumer (`verifySignature` in `message-send.ts:186`) would fail gracefully in its try/catch. Non-blocking.

**Item 2 -- `envelope.from` used as `ampAddress`:**
VERIFIED correct. `envelope.from` is the full AMP address (e.g., `alice@tenant.aimaestro.local`) per the `AMPEnvelope` interface at `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/types/amp.ts:117` which documents it as "Sender's AMP address: name@tenant.provider". This matches the `Message.amp.ampAddress` comment at line 65 ("Full AMP address (name@tenant.provider)"). Correct.

**Item 3 -- `envelopeId` uses raw vs normalized ID:**
VERIFIED intentional and correct. The PR uses `envelope.id` (raw) for `envelopeId`, not the normalized `id`. This is correct because `envelopeId` is documented as "Original AMP envelope ID" (line 66) -- it should preserve the original ID format (with underscores) for protocol fidelity, while the normalized `id` (with dashes) is used for internal deduplication. Good design.

**Item 4 -- Ternary condition `(envelope.signature || senderPublicKey)`:**
VERIFIED acceptable. Messages with only an `ampAddress` but no signature/key would get `amp: undefined`. This is correct behavior -- the `amp` field is specifically for "cryptographic verification data" (line 60 comment). An address-only message without crypto data does not need the `amp` block. The `ampAddress` info is already captured in `from`/`fromAlias`/`fromHost` fields.

**Item 5 -- UI/API consumers of `message.amp`:**
VERIFIED safe. Only two files read `message.amp`: `lib/message-send.ts` (lines 87, 172, 179, 186, 215-220, 298, 305) -- all use optional chaining (`message.amp?.signature`, etc.) so `undefined` is handled. No UI/component files (`.tsx`) reference `message.amp`. No breakage possible.

**Item 6 -- Tests:**
VERIFIED absent. No tests exist for `convertAMPToMessage` (searched `*.test.*` files). This is a pre-existing gap, not introduced by this PR. Non-blocking for this PR, but should be addressed separately.


</details>

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 20:58:10]*

Line 997 currently outputs: `   cd /path/to/dir` (unquoted). With the PR fix it would output: `   cd "/path/to/dir"`. Both are informational echo output within an already-double-quoted string -- there is no word-splitting risk here because the entire string is inside `echo "..."`. However, the fix adds visible quotes in the output, which is actually better for copy-paste if the path contains spaces.

Wait -- let me re-examine this. Line 997 is `echo "   cd $INSTALL_DIR"`. The `$INSTALL_DIR` here is inside a double-quoted string already. So there is NO word-splitting issue at all -- the variable expands correctly within the double quotes. The PR changes it to `echo "   cd \"$INSTALL_DIR\""` which changes the *output* from `cd /path/with spaces` to `cd "/path/with spaces"`. This is a UX improvement for copy-paste, not a bug fix.

Similarly, let me check line 991, 1022, 1024, 1039 -- all use `$INSTALL_DIR` inside double-quoted echo strings, which is already safe from word-splitting. The PR does NOT fix those. Let me confirm:

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 20:58:37]*

All five are inside double-quoted strings already. None have word-splitting issues. Only line 997 is a `cd` command that users would copy-paste, so adding visible quotes there is a UX improvement (the `cd` would fail in the user's shell if the path has spaces).

Now let me verify the line 293 fix is genuinely needed. `echo $NODE_VERSION` without quotes -- if `$NODE_VERSION` is empty, `echo` gets no arguments and outputs an empty line, then `cut` gets empty input. If `$NODE_VERSION` contains spaces (which `node --version` never does -- it returns e.g., `v20.11.0`), word splitting would occur. So the fix is correct but extremely low-risk since node version strings never contain spaces. Still, defensive quoting is best practice.

Now let me check the three `[ $MISSING_COUNT ...]` and `[ $TOOLS_INSTALLED ...]` usages -- these are unquoted integer variables in `[` test brackets. If the variable is empty/unset, this would cause a syntax error. However, both are always initialized before use (`MISSING_COUNT=0` at line 370, `TOOLS_INSTALLED=0` at line 845). Still, quoting is best practice per ShellCheck SC2086.

Let me now write the review output.

Here is my review:

---

**NEEDS WORK** -- PR #216 -- Both fixes are correct and improve the script, but the PR is incomplete: it fixes only 2 of 5 unquoted variable issues in the same file.

**Detailed findings:**

**Fix 1 (line 293): `echo $NODE_VERSION` to `echo "$NODE_VERSION"`** -- CORRECT. This is a genuine quoting bug (SC2086). The variable is outside of any enclosing double-quoted context, so word-splitting/globbing could theoretically apply. In practice `node --version` never returns spaces, but the fix follows shell best practices and is correct.

**Fix 2 (line 997): `echo "   cd $INSTALL_DIR"` to `echo "   cd \"$INSTALL_DIR\""`** -- CORRECT but mischaracterized. The `$INSTALL_DIR` was already inside a double-quoted `echo` string, so there was NO word-splitting bug here. What this fix actually does is add visible quotes in the *output* so that a user who copy-pastes `cd "/path/with spaces"` into their shell gets correct behavior. This is a UX improvement for paths with spaces, not a quoting bug fix. Good change, but the issue title is slightly misleading.

**Missing fixes the PR should also include:**

1. **Line 381:** `if [ $MISSING_COUNT -eq 0 ]` -- should be `"$MISSING_COUNT"` (SC2086). `MISSING_COUNT` is always initialized to 0, so no runtime risk, but it is the same class of issue the PR claims to fix.

2. **Line 388:** `if [ $MISSING_COUNT -gt 0 ]` -- same issue as line 381.

3. **Line 970:** `if [ $TOOLS_INSTALLED -gt 0 ]` -- same issue. `TOOLS_INSTALLED` is initialized to 0 at line 845.

These three are inside `[ ... ]` test brackets (not `[[ ... ]]`) where an unset/empty variable would cause a syntax error. They are initialized so no runtime risk exists, but they are the exact same ShellCheck SC2086 class that the PR's title targets.
